<div id="review_727549086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727549086" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727549086?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727549086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5089329974266590009"><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>This love triangle is different from others I have read because there isn’t a villain or an unworthy person in the equation. All three characters’ feelings are equal and relevant and although we are only privied to two povs throughout the story, the third person’s side is felt throughout.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>”It’s not so easy when you’re trying to win a war against the heart.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Ridge is a work at home computer guy who song writes for his brother’s band Sounds of Cedar. He is in a five year relationshi</span>
  <span id="freeText5089329974266590009" style="display:none"><span>[image error]</span><br><br>This love triangle is different from others I have read because there isn’t a villain or an unworthy person in the equation. All three characters’ feelings are equal and relevant and although we are only privied to two povs throughout the story, the third person’s side is felt throughout.<br><br><b>
  <i>”It’s not so easy when you’re trying to win a war against the heart.”</i>
</b><br><br>Ridge is a work at home computer guy who song writes for his brother’s band Sounds of Cedar. He is in a five year relationship with Maggie, a gorgeous and wonderful girl. A connection across a courtyard that progresses through the music that sweeps the apartment complex has Sydney under his spell. She has a love of music and is taken by Ridge’s talents and soon the two make contact.<br> <br><b>
  <i>”I can’t deny it,though. Anyone who watches how passionately this guy plays would crush on his talent.”</i>
</b><br><br>Sydney lives with her best friend Tori and is in a two year relationship with Hunter. When the betrayal of her best friend and boyfriend is revealed Ridge opens his apartment to her and two begin working on lyrics to Ridge’s music and they experience insane amounts of chemistry and both fight those feelings. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393844063i/8771365._SX540_.jpg" width="390" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ridge shares his apartment with Warren, Bridgette and now Sydney. Maggie visits regularly, Sydney and Ridge struggle with their building connection and feelings for one another (they create the most beautiful songs together), Warren and Bridgette get it on and then all of sudden BAM things get crazy. Of course there is a lot in between. Without spoiling anything, let me say I loved all the characters and disliked them at one point or another. This story has a big with the ending which I loved, but my feelings are still a bit all over the place.<br><br>I have conflicting feelings about how Ridge handled himself and his heart once he realizes it has been split in two. To be honest, I’m still thinking about this story and how I feel about it as a whole. The storyline was indeed unique and the characters truly tried to do the right thing. My issues weren't with Ridge’s feelings, perhaps his ingrained loyalty which may bother some readers more than me and some less than me. I would guess it’s up to the individual reader. Ridge truly was in a battle with his heart.<br><br>This is a story to be experienced and discussed with friends. I will definitely be swooning and ranting once this book is released with all of you! <br><br><b>Just read the epilogue on the author's page...Wow PEFECT ENDING!!! </b><br><br>Colleen Hoover, This story was painful and beautiful and unforgettable.<br><br>Simply put...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492337095ra/22506619.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>*ARC courtesy of Atria Books in exchange for an honest review*</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5089329974266590009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2041280837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041280837" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041280837?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=kindle-own">kindle-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041280837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10071386155849742209"><b>
  <blockquote>How can two people who both have such good intentions end up with feelings, derived from all the goodness, that are so incredibly bad?</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>I thought is book was really sweet. I mean there were a lot of things that got on my nerves but it all worked out in the end. <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498572741i/23138584._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>****SOME SPOILERS****<br/><br/>Sydney meets Ridge by listening to him play his guitar on his balcony every day. She sits on hers and he sits on his across the way. Ridge has been having trouble writing his lyrics for the band and he sees Sydney s</span>
  <span id="freeText10071386155849742209" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>How can two people who both have such good intentions end up with feelings, derived from all the goodness, that are so incredibly bad?</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I thought is book was really sweet. I mean there were a lot of things that got on my nerves but it all worked out in the end. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498572741i/23138584._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>****SOME SPOILERS****<br><br>Sydney meets Ridge by listening to him play his guitar on his balcony every day. She sits on hers and he sits on his across the way. Ridge has been having trouble writing his lyrics for the band and he sees Sydney singing to his music and thus it begins. <br><br>On Sydney's birthday she finds out from Ridge that her boyfriend of two years, Hunter, has been having a relationship with her roommate, Tori. He really didn't want to tell her but he couldn't put it off any longer. Ridge had seen them on the balcony. They say it was just sex and meant nothing, they had been having sex for years before they knew Syd. Seriously? <br><br>Anyway, Syd moves in with Ridge and his roommates, Bridgette and Warren. They are a hoot let me tell you. <br><br>Syd finds out Ridge is deaf but he can still play guitar and writes music for the band his brother formed. They are a big hit. Ridge won't play with them though because of his nerves and something else, but I won't tell you what that something else is, just something that is holding him back. <br><br>So Ridge and Syd communicate through text messages and the laptop. And they make music together. Syd writes the lyrics and Ridge plays, at least until he gets his muse back, which is through Sydney. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498572741ra/23138585.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498572741i/23138586._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then, Syd finds out Ridge has a girlfriend. Hello, you could have mentioned that from the beginning before I started falling for you. Men.<br><br>Maggie and Ridge have been together for 5 years and it's not all what it seems either. You know how you get comfortable with someone and they have other problems and you feel you can't leave them. But it all works out in the end for everyone. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498572741i/23138587._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved being able to read a nice fluffy book. Sometimes I just need to do that, although I don't need to explain myself to you. I enjoyed this book, but like I said I wanted to scream through some of it. I loved the characters and they all seemed to just get one another. Lovely.<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/06/maybe-someday-by-colleen-hoover.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/649750998?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer649750998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7562677605506669447"><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“Sometimes in life, we need a few bad days in order to keep the good ones in perspective.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971012._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This is my third book by Ms Hoover. I loved Hopeless. Was not too keen on Slammed. Yeah, saw all the rave reviews for this one and thought to myself will I? Still had a bit on the Amazon gift voucher…. Cos it’s not cheap for an e-book. You UK buyers are getting it for a bargain at your price. I buy on .com so it was a bit more.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“Hey, heart. Are you listening?<br/>You and I are officially at war.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971014._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I saw the</span>
  <span id="freeText7562677605506669447" style="display:none"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Sometimes in life, we need a few bad days in order to keep the good ones in perspective.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971012._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is my third book by Ms Hoover. I loved Hopeless. Was not too keen on Slammed. Yeah, saw all the rave reviews for this one and thought to myself will I? Still had a bit on the Amazon gift voucher…. Cos it’s not cheap for an e-book. You UK buyers are getting it for a bargain at your price. I buy on .com so it was a bit more.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Hey, heart. Are you listening?<br>You and I are officially at war.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971014._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I saw the reviews but I did not read them and I am so glad I didn’t as this book was a complete surprise for me. And a pleasant one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395241952i/8971223._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So I don’t want to say too much about the book for fear of giving anything away. It was very emotional. I really did not know which way it was going…. I felt I was holding my breath for the last 20% of the book. But I ended up LOVING it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I...will never...regret you.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971015._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Another reason I wasn’t going to read this is at is NA. He is 24 and she is 22. But it did not read like an NA book. It was just a good book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“A life of mediocrity is a waste of a life.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Like Colleen, I love music so this book had the added bonus of having music throughout it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971016._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I don't want to care. But I can tell by how disappointed I feel that I do care.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971017._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“There will never be a maybe someday.”</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395239985i/8971018.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586230076" />
    <a title="Kayla at MyBookMuse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10212063-kayla-at-mybookmuse"><img alt="Kayla at MyBookMuse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412025796p2/10212063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586230076?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla at MyBookMuse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla at MyBookMuse" href="/user/show/10212063-kayla-at-mybookmuse">Kayla at MyBookMuse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586230076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11071341382655890025">REVIEW:<br/><br/>There is no doubt that Colleen Hoover can write any amazing novel. The development and interaction between Sydney and Ridge was pure magic. Their method of communicating with each other felt like a language meant only for Sydney and Ridge and I felt like a fly on the wall playing witness to their romance. One of elements of this novel that I appreciated was the lyrics. I usually cringe when I read lyrics in books because they come off so cheesy and unrealistic but not with Maybe Someday. </span>
  <span id="freeText11071341382655890025" style="display:none">REVIEW:<br><br>There is no doubt that Colleen Hoover can write any amazing novel. The development and interaction between Sydney and Ridge was pure magic. Their method of communicating with each other felt like a language meant only for Sydney and Ridge and I felt like a fly on the wall playing witness to their romance. One of elements of this novel that I appreciated was the lyrics. I usually cringe when I read lyrics in books because they come off so cheesy and unrealistic but not with Maybe Someday. Romantic. Heartbreaking. And uplifting. This book is a must read! <br><br>4.5 STARS<br><br>*I received an ARC from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review**<br><br>Based off previous Colleen Hoover novels I will:<br><br>1. Cry<br>2. Fall in love<br>3. Have a new book boyfriend <br><br><a href="http://www.mybookmuse.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/tumblr_mim3n3QXWi1qe5w4eo1_500.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="tumblr_mim3n3QXWi1qe5w4eo1_500" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417031i/824311.jpg" width="500" height="333" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Get ready mystery man, we are coming for you!<br></span>

<div id="review_689029120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689029120" />
    <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish"><img alt="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405178063p2/5614985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689029120?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish">Hazel (Stay Bookish)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=own-copy-read">own-copy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=2014-lovelies">2014-lovelies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689029120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2457593188909746553">Originally posted at <a href='http://staybookish.net/review-maybe-someday-colleen-hoover/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stay Bookish</a><br/><br/>Here’s the thing: I’m a huge fan of Colleen Hoover- a tremendously HUGE fan. I’m in love with everything she writes and I’d basically buy anything she puts her name on. Colleen is high on my favorite author list and I’ve adored every single one of her books, especially this latest one, Maybe Someday.<br/><br/>Saying I was excited to read Maybe Someday would be quite the understatement. I basically counted down the days until it was released and no one would ever understand</span>
  <span id="freeText2457593188909746553" style="display:none">Originally posted at <a href="http://staybookish.net/review-maybe-someday-colleen-hoover/" rel="nofollow noopener">Stay Bookish</a><br /><br />Here’s the thing: I’m a huge fan of Colleen Hoover- a tremendously HUGE fan. I’m in love with everything she writes and I’d basically buy anything she puts her name on. Colleen is high on my favorite author list and I’ve adored every single one of her books, especially this latest one, Maybe Someday.<br /><br />Saying I was excited to read Maybe Someday would be quite the understatement. I basically counted down the days until it was released and no one would ever understand how ecstatic I was when I found out it had been already available at my local bookstore. I was not only thrilled that it was a Colleen Hoover book, but also that it had aspects I was interested in, like music and romance. The book focuses respectively on Sydney and Ridge, the female and male lead, who both have their own POVs. Their story is one of a kind- it’s incredibly heartbreaking, but most of all, beautifully told.<br /><br /><i>Sometimes in life, we need a few bad days in order to keep the good ones in perspective.</i><br /><br />The novel starts with Sydney, who just turned twenty-two and was having the suckiest day of her life. Betrayed by her best friend and boyfriend, Sydney was angry, depressed, and was left with nowhere to go. From the very first line of the book, I knew Sydney was going to be a very readable character for me. If there was one thing I loved about her the most, it was that she kept things real. Her dialogues with the people around her were fun, her internal conflicts were so relatable and honest and she was a really good heroine in general.<br /><br />In the midst of the disaster that is her life, Sydney finds a friend in her enigmatic musician neighbor, Ridge, and convinces herself that she’s only crushing on his guitar talents. I’m not even sure how to begin describing Ridge. He took me completely by surprise. I did not expect him to be how he is (those who’ve read will understand what I mean!) but I loved that Colleen Hoover made her male lead different from the rest and also so completely layered. I loved reading about Ridge’s disposition when it came to music- it was so interesting to look at things through his perspective. Aside from that, I loved his personality in general, how he is passionate and caring and also how he loves pranks!<br /><br /><i>I’ve learned that the heart can’t be told when and who and how it should love. The heart does whatever the hell it wants to do. The only thing we can control is whether we give our lives and our minds the chance to catch up to our hearts.</i><br /><br />Ridge has been having a block when it came to writing lyrics so he collaborates with Sydney, who is utterly passionate about songs and music. The two grow attracted to each other but they establish a deeper connection more than just a physical one. However, Ridge has Maggie, his girlfriend, and that meant he and Sydney couldn’t and shouldn’t act on their feelings. I love that Maggie was not viewed as an antagonist of the story even though she was the reason Sydney and Ridge couldn’t be together and all. She was actually really wonderful and nice and you can see why Ridge loves her very much. Ridge’s best friend, Warren, was also a great minor character! I came to adore him during the entirety of the book, not only because he was pretty hilarious, but also because he was so frank and honest.<br /><br />If I may be honest as well, I found Maybe Someday to be very conflicting- but in a really good “ahh omg feeeeels” kind of way! After all, the story revolves around a relationship that is wrong in the context of the situation but nonetheless feels so right, which I must say is totally confusing and frustrating, not just for the characters, but also for the reader (in this case: me), whose emotions become one with Ridge and Sydney’s. With Colleen Hoover’s expert writing, she manages to show us that there is more to these kinds of circumstances. It’s not about what’s right or wrong, it’s about the feelings that are there and about what the main characters choose to do about it. I loved how the two were both so mature, how they really tried so hard to fight their hearts and it tore me apart, seeing them struggle with their feelings so much.<br /><br /><i>People don’t get to choose who they fall in love with. They only get to choose who they stay in love with.</i><br /><br />Not only was this book heart wrenching, it was also fascinating, what with the aspect of music and lyrics bringing Sydney and Ridge together. If there’s one thing that gets me as emotional as books do, it’s music. I have to say: my favorite part of this whole novel would be the lyrics. Every word was just so perfect for every scene, every emotion, and I just loved it beyond everything else. A gorgeous soundtrack accompanies Maybe Someday and it contains the songs Sydney and Ridge wrote for and about each other. Listening to the soundtrack album while reading the respective scenes was the best thing ever! I’ve never had such an unforgettable reading experience until this one!<br /><br />All in all, I really loved Maybe Someday. It was poignant and thought provoking, not to mention a breath of fresh air compared to most of the books in this genre. Maybe Someday may be Colleen’s most complicated book yet but it’s also her most profound book so far. Sure to impress its readers, Maybe Someday brims with heart and hope.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2457593188909746553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=traveling-frends-summer-reading-cha">traveling-frends-summer-reading-cha</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2942660784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17034645368889320664">Colleen Hoover can write books that I get quickly absorbed in and can't read fast enough. This book was no exception. I couldn't put it down while at the same time wanting to pull the two main characters aside and give them a serious talking to. The long and short of it is, Sydney finds out that her boyfriend has been cheating with her best friend who is also her roommate. She leaves and is quickly given a place to stay by Ridge, the man who she listens to play guitar at night. They bond over a </span>
  <span id="freeText17034645368889320664" style="display:none">Colleen Hoover can write books that I get quickly absorbed in and can't read fast enough. This book was no exception. I couldn't put it down while at the same time wanting to pull the two main characters aside and give them a serious talking to. The long and short of it is, Sydney finds out that her boyfriend has been cheating with her best friend who is also her roommate. She leaves and is quickly given a place to stay by Ridge, the man who she listens to play guitar at night. They bond over a love of music and spend time together working on lyrics and never, not once, does he divulge an important fact to her......How could that have possibly slipped his mind.<br /><br />Anyway, I enjoyed most of the characters and was sucked in, I completely understand why some people had issues with this book. For me this was a very nice rebound book (get it) after reading a not so great book. It was nice to sink into a book and be completely captivated. Plus, I enjoyed reading both main character's POV chapters. It was nice to read what was going on in each of their heads. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" href="/user/show/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei">Lady Vigilante (Feifei)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686233577" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3603332592928033122">Go get it!! >> <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/1i6jCev'>http://amzn.to/1i6jCev</a> <<<br/><br/>If you've read this already, go <a href='http://www.maybesomedaysoundtrack.com/bonus.php' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a> for the epilogue written in a secondary character's POV. Password is the last word of the last chapter of the book. <br/><br/><b>4 STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393822037i/8769111._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Without a doubt, this book dealt a powerful blow to my feels and is one of the most emotionally charged stories I’ve read this year! Whenever I see a Colleen Hoover book, I know to brace myself for a story that builds up in intensity and showcases unique plot twists. Her stories are always so well-w</span>
  <span id="freeText3603332592928033122" style="display:none">Go get it!! &gt;&gt; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1i6jCev">http://amzn.to/1i6jCev</a> &lt;&lt;<br><br>If you've read this already, go <a href="http://www.maybesomedaysoundtrack.com/bonus.php" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> for the epilogue written in a secondary character's POV. Password is the last word of the last chapter of the book. <br><br><b>4 STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393822037i/8769111._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Without a doubt, this book dealt a powerful blow to my feels and is one of the most emotionally charged stories I’ve read this year! Whenever I see a Colleen Hoover book, I know to brace myself for a story that builds up in intensity and showcases unique plot twists. Her stories are always so well-written (at least for me) and she knows how to make the little things count. She doesn’t trivialize. She doesn’t exaggerate. She delivers. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393822037i/8769112._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sydney Blake has the perfect life: an attentive boyfriend Hunter, doing well in college, BFFs with Tori, etc…but on what should’ve been a fantastic, special day for her turns into her worst nightmare as she discovers Hunter has been cheating on her with Tori. <br><br>****MINOR SPOILER****<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay so this is where I had a little problem. From the blurb I expected Sydney to be connecting with Ridge on a musical level <i>after</i> she finds out about Hunter and Tori, but she actually knows and chats with him beforehand. Not a bad thing, but the way it was introduced into the story i.e. the book structure (present, then flashback) cut my reading flow a little. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>****END OF SPOILER****<br><br>Sydney has this special connection with Ridge that goes beyond their mutual love of music. There’s no name to it, but it’s a feeling you’ll experience when you read it because it’s so passionately and tenderly palpable. <br><br>Now you’re wondering okay, so what’s the <i>story?</i> Is it just them falling in love over making music? No it’s not, and normally I’m inclined to disclose details but this is one of the rare times I feel you should go into the book as blind as possible. But for those that just need a little more to go off of, this next section is for you. <br><br>****DETAILS IF YOU NEED MORE****<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There’s no way to fluff it so I’m just going to say it: there is a love triangle so this story is essentially a forbidden romance. However, it was impossible for me to NOT appreciate the love triangle aspect as it’s so real and heartfelt and <b>there is no bad guy.</b> I’ll admit, it was a damn struggle to read 75% of the book because what these characters were going through wasn’t contrived or added in as a filler, but sensational and <b>honest.</b> It was how they felt and their natural response to these feelings. For me, reading this book was like opening a Pandora box full of emotions and letting those emotions smack me in the face over and over again. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393822037i/8769113._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While I actually enjoyed the love triangle aspect, it was the conclusion/ending of the triangle that brought down my rating. For me, the magic of Colleen Hoover’s writing is its spontaneity and unpredictability, and the fact that I can never really pinpoint what will happen next. Somewhere along the way, the unpredictable became predictable and that took away from the originality and thrill of reading Sydney and Ridge’s story. I’m not saying I hated the way Ridge “chose” one of the two girls, but it ruined the uniqueness of the love triangle aspect and no matter how well-written it was, I was left feeling underwhelmed. From this point of the book to the ending, I was pretty much done and felt the book should’ve ended, but it dragged on instead. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>****END OF DETAILS****<br><br>Another thing I’m starting to notice in many NA books (and in this book too) is the slut-shaming of practically every female character but the heroine. I don’t usually point this out unless it really bothers me and it did. I genuinely liked Sydney but the time where she calls Tori a bitch (which she deserves) and then immediately after sees another girl in a Hooters uniform and thinks <b>
  <i>“I don't know why she's complaining about getting wet, when there isn't much clothing to get wet.”</i>
</b> and calls her a bitch annoyed me. Putting the name of “Barbie” on Tori I think was supposed to be humorous, but I felt like it was used as a distinction between our good girl heroine and bad girl, punishment-deserving female characters. Quite honestly, the book could’ve omitted that part because Sydney <i>is</i> a great heroine; I never felt the need for any justification to why I shouldn’t like her. <br><br>I had originally planned on giving this book 3.5 stars because the problems I stated above were a raging forefront in my mind, but after a night’s sleep I realized that the emotional intensity and good writing quality were what stood out to me more than any of the problems so it’s a 4 star read. Though I can’t say I fully enjoyed the book, it’s truly an unforgettable story; that point is undeniable. <br><br><i>ARC provided by publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><b>For more reviews, freebie lists, &amp; giveaways visit my blog!</b><br><a href="http://bookvigilantereviews.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394737586i/8898309._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1061999903?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061999903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3509158603920061827">2.5 stars<br/><br/>I'm slowly beginning to think that Colleen Hoover just isn't for me. I don't understand the hype behind her whatsoever. The only good thing about this book was that it was fast-paced. That, and it had a cool twist that would be a spoiler to tell you, but if you've read it, you know what I mean and I really liked that aspect of it. But this book was just entirely too angsty. I hate that cheating is such a common trope used in New Adult, and although it may be realistic, it's OBNOXIOUS. I</span>
  <span id="freeText3509158603920061827" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />I'm slowly beginning to think that Colleen Hoover just isn't for me. I don't understand the hype behind her whatsoever. The only good thing about this book was that it was fast-paced. That, and it had a cool twist that would be a spoiler to tell you, but if you've read it, you know what I mean and I really liked that aspect of it. But this book was just entirely too angsty. I hate that cheating is such a common trope used in New Adult, and although it may be realistic, it's OBNOXIOUS. If you cheat on your girlfriend, tell her and deal with the consequences and stop crying literally every 3 pages for half of this book. This book had no other plot other than a sob story about cheating and regret. Colleen Hoover loves including small phrases like "she hits like a girl" and "i need her to be vulnerable" (actual lines pulled from Ridge's POV), which totally rubbed me the wrong way. I just hate how Colleen Hoover tackles these serious problems and over-dramatizes them. By the end I was ready for this to be done so that there would stop being so much ridiculous angst. <br /><br />Additionally, I wasn't a fan of the soundtrack for this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3509158603920061827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2014039995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ninoska Goris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52598215-ninoska-goris"><img alt="Ninoska Goris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578758582p2/52598215.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6585378541185078703">English - Español<br/><br/>With this book two totally new things are given to me: a love triangle with two women and a man and a protagonist who is deaf.<br/><br/>The strangest thing about Ridge is that he plays the guitar and composes songs, music and lyrics.   <span id="freeText6585378541185078703" style="display:none">English - Español<br /><br />With this book two totally new things are given to me: a love triangle with two women and a man and a protagonist who is deaf.<br /><br />The strangest thing about Ridge is that he plays the guitar and composes songs, music and lyrics. It's lovely to see him with Maggie, but it's also lovely to see him with Sydney. They are two people who blend very well, something like your soul mate if it were in an ideal world. The stories of how he and his little brother Brennan grew up are simply heartbreaking and inspiring at the same time.<br /><br />His life was tough since childhood with abusive parents, unconcerned and ashamed of his deafness, having to practically raise Brennan. But now he has his brother and his best friend Warren, who is like another brother and my favorite character in this book.<br /><br />Sydney, oh Sydney, is my least favorite of all in the book, including Bridgette. I don't identify with her in absolutely nothing. First, when she is without a boyfriend and homeless she prefers being under the rain sitting in her suitcases than going up to look for her wallet, staying in an apartment where she doesn't know anyone, falling in love with a man who has girlfriend and who has told her that he isn't going to leave her and have the nerve to tell him that they can't be together now because he just finished with Maggie when she not only liked Ridge since she had a boyfriend, but just several weeks of finishing with Hunter was already falling in love with Ridge and the worst is that she spend most of half book crying. <br /><br />Despite Sydney and that many things happen that can be considered as infidelity, I liked the book. It goes fast, it doesn't bore and it ends like it has to end.<br /><br />The next book in this series is of Warren and I coudn't be happier.<br /><br />✨✨✨<br /><br />Con este libro se dan dos cosas totalmente nuevas para mí: un triángulo amoroso con dos mujeres y un hombre y un protagonista que es sordo.<br /><br />Lo más extraño de Ridge es que toca la guitarra y compone canciones, música y letra. Es adorable verlo con Maggie, pero también es adorable verlo con Sydney. Son dos personas que se compenetran muy bien, algo así como tu alma gemela si fuera en un mundo ideal. Las historias de cómo crecieron el y su hermano Brennan son simplemente desgarradoras e inspiradoras al mismo tiempo.<br /><br />Ha pasado mucho trabajo desde pequeño con unos padres abusivos, despreocupados y avergonzados de su sordera, teniendo que prácticamente criar a Brennan. Pero ahora cuenta con su hermano y con su mejor amigo Warren, quién es como otro hermano y mi personaje favorito de este libro.<br /><br />Sydney, oh Sydney, es mi menos favorita de todos los que aparecen en el libro, incluyendo a Bridgette. No me identifico con ella en absolutamente nada. Primeramente cuando se queda sin novio y sin casa prefiere pasar trabajo, como estar bajo lluvia sentada en sus maletas que subir a buscar su cartera, quedarse a vivir en un apartamento donde no conoce a nadie, enamorarse de un hombre que tiene su novia y que le ha dicho que no la va a dejar y tener la desfachatez de decirle que no pueden estar juntos ahora porque el acaba de terminar con Maggie cuando a ella no solo le gustaba Ridge desde que tenía novio, sino que apenas varias semanas de terminar con Hunter ya se estaba enamorando de Ridge y lo peor de todo es que se pasa medio libro llorando. <br /><br />A pesar de Sydney y de que pasan muchas cosas que se pueden considerar como una infidelidad, el libro me gustó. Va rápido, no aburre y termina como tiene que terminar.<br /><br />El próximo libro de esta serie es de Warren y no puedo estar más feliz.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13697155975347204650"><b>
  <i>Maybe Someday</i>
</b> is another home run from Colleen Hoover, leaving me sniffling and teary-eyed!! (This has become a regular occurrence when reading her books!)<br/><br/>From the moment she seems him playing the guitar on his apartment balcony, something about Ridge mesmerizes Sydney. He’s handsome, sure, but he has an indescribable appeal which, coupled with his talent, draws Sydney out on to her balcony across the way so she can listen to him play. She's embarrassed to admit this to her best friend and r</span>
  <span id="freeText13697155975347204650" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Maybe Someday</i>
</b> is another home run from Colleen Hoover, leaving me sniffling and teary-eyed!! (This has become a regular occurrence when reading her books!)<br /><br />From the moment she seems him playing the guitar on his apartment balcony, something about Ridge mesmerizes Sydney. He’s handsome, sure, but he has an indescribable appeal which, coupled with his talent, draws Sydney out on to her balcony across the way so she can listen to him play. She's embarrassed to admit this to her best friend and roommate, so she just pretends to study on the balcony a lot.<br /><br />When Ridge notices Sydney singing words to the songs which don’t exist, he seeks her help with lyrics. Since she has a serious boyfriend, they just text back and forth, and songs are born.<br /><br />One night everything falls apart for Sydney when she discovers her boyfriend and her roommate have been sleeping together. Ridge sweeps in to help his valuable lyricist and she temporarily moves in with him and his roommates. But what ensues is far more complex, intense, and emotional than it seems on the surface, leaving both of them to decide what path is the right one to take.<br /><br />"How can two good people who both have such good intentions end up with feelings, derived from all the goodness, that are so incredibly bad?"<br /><br />This book surprised me with a few of the twists Hoover threw in. They really brought a fascinating and utterly compelling perspective to the book and the love stories within it. <b>
  <i>Maybe Someday</i>
</b> is super steamy at times, utterly poignant at others, and it really makes you wonder how even with the best of intentions you can hurt someone else so deeply.<br /><br />I’ve become an enormous CoHo fan, having read five or six of her books in the last several months. I need to keep diving into her backlist! Any recommendations on which book of hers to read next?<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2019 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html</a>. <br /><br />Check out my list of the best books of the decade at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html</a>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>

  <span id="freeText16059771886654557695" style="display:none"><b>4 Beautiful Stars.</b>	<br><br>Sydney finds out that her boyfriend of two years is a cheater so she accepts help from her neighbor, Ridge. <br>Ridge and Sydney connect trough music and soon very strong feelings starts to develop between them. <br>But life always gets in the way and things aren’t always easy: there will be major obstacles, hearts they don’t want to break… and heartbreaking beautiful songs. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395014130ra/8935685.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me just start by saying that I love Colleen Hoover. Exactly how Colleen got us used to. <br>And even in this crazy book where everything could go wrong, she turned it in a way that will make us end this reading with happy tears flooding from our eyes. <br> <b>Character Development: </b> Sydney is pretty good and I love how respectful she is to the other parts in all this messed up situation.     <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604243806?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nicholas Sparks fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sweet-guy">sweet-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve">bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=college">college</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604243806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4555449423407640558"><i>
  <b>2 STARS<br/><blockquote>People don’t get to choose who they fall in love with. They only get to choose who they stay in love with.</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>Well if there’s one good thing I can say about Colleen Hoover at this point in my reading canon, there is something about the way she writes that allows me to finish her book in a day. There’s an ease in the way she tells a story, a manner that keeps my attention even when I don’t like what is going on. I can’t seem to look away, even when half the time I’m alternating between wan</span>
  <span id="freeText4555449423407640558" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>2 STARS<br><blockquote>People don’t get to choose who they fall in love with. They only get to choose who they stay in love with.</blockquote></b>
</i><br>Well if there’s one good thing I can say about Colleen Hoover at this point in my reading canon, there is something about the way she writes that allows me to finish her book in a day. There’s an ease in the way she tells a story, a manner that keeps my attention even when I don’t like what is going on. I can’t seem to look away, even when half the time I’m alternating between wanting to smack and throttle the protagonists senseless.<br><br><u>
  <b>INSTA-BLURB:</b>
</u>Sydney is forced to leave the apartment she shares with her friend Tori upon discovering that she occasionally hits up her boyfriend, Hunter, for meaningless sex. Penniless, purseless and jobless, she finds herself squatting with Ridge, the cute musician from the apartment across who has convinced her to write lyrics for him as rent after he sees her singing along his impromptu balcony concerts. This of course leads to writing sessions that don’t really end up as writing sessions as Ridge and Sydney start to feel a forbidden attraction towards each other. <br><br>Basically, <i>Maybe Someday</i> is a 367-kindle pages guide on how to rationalize infidelity. How to justify falling for your writing partner while being in love with your girlfriend who, because this wouldn’t be a Hoover book if not, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[suffers from a deadly disease that will kill her before she reaches the age of 30. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It’s pages and pages of guilt, conflicting emotions, jealousy and guilt over being jealous. A lengthy introspection on love and hearts within hearts, and hearts being halved and a valiant attempt at trying to portray the concept of loving more than one person in a mature and dignified manner. It felt a lot like it was trying to sell me this product, pointing out the good and the bad, giving balanced perspectives through alternating POVs between Sydney and Ridge…<br><br>…only to draw the conclusion that the answer is in listening to one’s heartbeat.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396409413ra/9129543.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don’t know, it just ended up being too Hallmark treacly for me. Initially I was sold on the originality of choosing a deaf musician for a hero. I mean, who would rage on a guy who is simultaneously sweet, sensitive and hell bent on being faithful to his girlfriend? I was wary that his deafness opens an avenue ripe for emotional exploitation. Well this kind of did and did not. A lot of his and Sydney’s scenes together seem to be written around that particular detail and most of their tender moments used that as an emotional crutch, so to speak. So when the whole Maggie subplot was brought into the picture, it just got a little over the top, dramatic gimmickry for me.<br><br>And since I don’t know how to lead into this thought, I’m just going to come out and say it: <b>I did not get the Maggie love.</b> I’m a heartless monster, I know. But apart from Ridge, Warren and Sydney saying so, why again is she awesome? Atleast the emotional manipulation from Ridge’s character is subtle, Maggie was just too in-your-face for my tastes. To be clear, it’s not just the Nicholas Sparksing of Maggie that didn’t sit right with me, I felt she was poorly explored as a character outside of her and Ridge’s story, making it difficult for me to appreciate her distinctly from him. <br><br>There was so much angst going on, the book somehow forgot to illustrate the happiness any of these characters derive from each other. From where I stand, everyone would probably be better off single. <br><br>It feels a bit strange complaining about that in a Colleen Hoover book. Though it’s been a while since I last read an original story from her, I remember that she writes particularly endearing interludes between her protagonists. She has a knack for writing in charm in the banter between her leads and in her secondary characters that subtly compliments the heavy drama in her climactic scenes. I find myself missing Kiersten’s wit in all that Pine-Sol and Warrenisms.<br><br>Despite all of that, I would’ve still given this a 3-star rating. <br><br>Had it not been for Sydney.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Him: Do you sing in the shower?<br><br>I shake my head, confirming my initial suspicion. He’s a flirt. Of course he is, he’s a musician.<br><br>Me: I don’t know what kind of question that is, but if this is your attempt at flirting, I’ve got a boyfriend. Don’t waste your time.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>That’s the exact point that I knew I am not going to be a fan of this girl. There’s a certain kind of presumptuousness from her that rubbed me wrong in that exchange. I have guy friends who’ve relayed anecdotes similar to this one and most of them ended with “I have a girlfriend too, I’m actually not hitting on you believe it or not.”<br><br>I’m supposed to like her better because she spends a great deal of time being morally conflicted with her feelings for Ridge and her experience with Hunter. But the way she phrases her thoughts in her POVs runs a whole roller coaster of annoying to <b>ANNOYING</b>:<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>✔︎ I’m happy that he’s here. I’m pissed off that he’s here.<br>✔︎ Please, let it be Ridge. Please, don’t let it be Ridge.<br>✔︎ I’ve never felt about anyone or anything the way I feel about him.<br>✔︎ Oh, my God he looks incredible. It’s the first time I’ve ever seen him on a stage.<br>✔︎ I love the fact that Hunter is about to turn around and witness Ridge looking like this. (i.e. Shirtless.)</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>It cheapens an already shallow character, one that fit so incongruously in a story that already struggles with keeping up the appearances of being a New Adult Contemporary Romance of depth. <br><br>Once upon a time I thought <i>Slammed</i> was the best book I’ve ever read. <br><br>I’ve read everything Colleen Hoover has written ever since, in the hopes that I can recapture that first read high. I can see her evolution as a writer. But I’m not quite sure I’m evolving in the same path with her anymore.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>We both know where we want to be; we just don’t know how to get there. <br>Or when we should get there.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/839206/heartception" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4555449423407640558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1440794080" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1440794080" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1440794080?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=blue-ballin">blue-ballin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=zero-dollars-makes-me-holler">zero-dollars-makes-me-holler</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1440794080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15695765929682633811">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>A 4.38 average on Goodreads, you say? Yeah, that sounds about par for the course on books I rate 1 Star. Now, before everyone goes all cuckoo crazy I need to ask a favor . . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049446.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Don’t tar and feather me just yet. I’m actually one of you and have fangirled over CoHo in the past (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342263082?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>EXHIBIT A</a>). In fact, the only story I <i>didn’t</i> like was <i>Never Never</i> and that was more because it was a serial (which I <b>hate</b>) and it didn’t have enough sto</span>
  <span id="freeText15695765929682633811" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>A 4.38 average on Goodreads, you say? Yeah, that sounds about par for the course on books I rate 1 Star. Now, before everyone goes all cuckoo crazy I need to ask a favor . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049446.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Don’t tar and feather me just yet. I’m actually one of you and have fangirled over CoHo in the past (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342263082?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">EXHIBIT A</a>). In fact, the only story I <i>didn’t</i> like was <i>Never Never</i> and that was more because it was a serial (which I <b>hate</b>) and it didn’t have enough storyline in part one to keep me interested in obtaining a copy of part 2.<br><br>I didn’t like one diddly dang dong thing about <i>Maybe Someday</i>, though, and it began immediately with a tired trope that was just not cool with me . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049447.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Again, put the buckets of pig blood down. This tired trope <b>has</b> worked for me in the past (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396175963?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">EXHIBIT B </a>). It just has to be done the right way <i>for me</i>. <b>THIS</b> might be (and judging by the ratings obviously was) the right way for most everyone else. <br><br>When Sydney discovers her live-in boyfriend has been banging her bestie on the side, she finds herself jobless and homeless. Left out in the rain with nowhere to go, neighbor Ridge saves the day. Ridge and Sydney have been “communicating” via music through the courtyard for a bit, which has also given Ridge a front-row seat for the “extracurricular activities” Sydney’s significant other has been dabbling in on the side. He feels sorry for her so he (and his roommates) offer Sydney a place to stay. Soon Ridge discovers Sydney has a flair for writing song lyrics – something he has always done until a severe case of writer’s block kicked in. Working so closely together, it doesn’t take long for the two to realize they have an undeniable attraction to each other. But Ridge has a long-term girlfriend . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049448.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Therein lies the rub. What exactly constitutes cheating? Well, as far as I’m concerned if I found my out my husband/boyfriend/whatever was spending his evenings lying in bed, making sweet, sweet music with another chick and due to . . . . <i>reasons</i> found it necessary to do things like wrap his arms around her or rest his hand across her heaving bosom in order to really “feeeeeeel” the music I’d probably react kinda like this . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049449.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And as soon as Sydney said <b>
  <i>“I will never, ever do that to another girl”</i>
</b> - followed by locking lips with Ridge I knew I was going to get more than a lil’ bit ragey. Unfortunately . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049450.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But enough about that. Let’s move on to the other thing that ruined this book for me – the music. While I appreciate CoHo’s use of “mixed media” in her stories (<b>especially</b> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1233341746?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">EXHIBIT C</a>), it didn’t work for me this time around. The lyrics were super cheese-a-riffic and the whole idea really jumped the shark once I discovered there was a song entitled “Trouble” . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049451.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I thought maybe it was just a case of needing the music rather than just reading the words so I took a couple of minutes to You Tube the songs themselves and hear what they sounded like. What I discovered? Nah, nah honey I’m good. I can definitely live without any of those on my iTunes playlist. (Please note I’m also a middle-aged woman who doesn’t like Adele. I should probably burn myself at the stake.) When I hear that songs are supposed to make me feely, they need to be <b>feeeely</b>. However, the feels I like to feel are things like anger : )<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe that's what happens when a tornado meets a volcano<br>All I know is I love you too much to walk away though<br>Come inside, pick up your bags off the sidewalk<br>Don't you hear sincerity in my voice when I talk<br>Told you this is my fault<br>Look me in the eyeball<br>Next time I'm pissed, I'll aim my fist at the drywall<br>Next time? There won't be no next time!<br>I apologize even though I know its lies<br>I'm tired of the games I just want her back<br>I know I'm a liar<br>If she ever tries to fucking leave again<br>Im'a tie her to the bed and set this house on fire.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Yeah, I’m nuts. Don’t get it twisted that I think that is a “sexy” song, though, ‘cause it’s not. The video on the other hand . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049452.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Aruuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuuga!<br><br>The point I’m trying to make is that it stirs <b>emotion</b> and these songs didn’t. I don’t want to make with the sexy to whiny crybaby songs by Bieber (only Erica gets off on that). I want to do the dirty to The Weekend . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049453.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, at least I did until it nearly got ruined for me by having a track added to the <i>50 Shades</i> soundtrack. Then (much like with the "romance" in this book), my snatch was all like . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049454.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Bottom line is I hated this story (I know I was pretty vague up there so you might have had a hard time reading between the lines), but I’m still a fan of CoHo. Not every book works for every reader. Luckily at Goodreads you have the ability to read <b>tons</b> of different personal opinions (NONE of which are wrong). This one was already on your TBR? <b>Definitely</b> still read it. It wasn’t, but now you’re intrigued? Add it to the TBR. Hate that my opinion differs from yours and now you’re butthurt????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447779242ra/17049455.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ha! I keeeeeed. Well, kind of. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15695765929682633811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1220449375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220449375" />
    <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland"><img alt="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560365354p2/21937982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_650288736" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650288736" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650288736?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia Ramírez" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez">Claudia Ramírez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476753164" href="/book/show/18143950-maybe-someday">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650288736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8908450010534006625">Review to come later. For now, I just have to say that Warren was my favorite character <3. Also, that it bothered me a little that Sydney spent half of the book crying. I'm not even joking, she was always crying! <br/><br/>Anyways. I really liked this book <3.<br/><br/>LATER (as in two days later):<br/><br/>OK, I'm finally ready to review this. I'll be brief. First of all, I love Colleen Hoover and this book didn't let me down <3. The writing was just as beautiful as always and the characters were endearing. I didn't expect</span>
  <span id="freeText8908450010534006625" style="display:none">Review to come later. For now, I just have to say that Warren was my favorite character &lt;3. Also, that it bothered me a little that Sydney spent half of the book crying. I'm not even joking, she was always crying! <br /><br />Anyways. I really liked this book &lt;3.<br /><br />LATER (as in two days later):<br /><br />OK, I'm finally ready to review this. I'll be brief. First of all, I love Colleen Hoover and this book didn't let me down &lt;3. The writing was just as beautiful as always and the characters were endearing. I didn't expect THAT <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rigde was deaf! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> thing about Ridge. When he made the revelation (early in the book) I was SO bewildered! I don't know, maybe it is because I had never read book with a main character (and narrator!) with that condition (until this book, anyway). <br /><br />I really loved Ridge... there were times when I wanted to punch him, but overall he was an amazing guy that made my heart explode with love (and he also broke it a few times!). Sydney was also likeable, but not my favorite. As I said before, she was always crying! She was happy: she cried. She was sad: She cried. She was angry: She cried. UGH, sometimes I was just like: "OK SYD, that's enough!" But she didn't stop. Also, I loved Warren... at first I thought he was a jerk, but OH, he's the best friend Sydney and Ridge could ever ask for!<br /><br />I'm glad with the way things ended in this book. Ridge had a difficult choice to make and I think that Maggie helped him a lot with that.<br /><br />Also, I teared up <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[every time Ridge spoke to Sydney. OH GOD, I couldn't handle it! Those scenes where so heart wrenching and BEAUTIFUL! Every word Ridge spoke to Sydney was beautiful and perfect and made me cry like a baby. Really, my FEELS where all over the place! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />And hmmm... I think that is all (?), haha. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8908450010534006625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24920901-the-deal"><img alt="The Deal (Off-Campus, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1431282052l/24920901._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iJ7qmUJHMTXLw2qF6Ks93HsA8B+rDcanRKgL7MYRjHFPARdAOBzfovPXIih9qWU6E+Ea/Ro3fC+wa/JRnib2kg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2xUpezjZg3Ekjr8xgsUMB2k2hE66yTPYrTOwoCOMd+scitSiQoJt5hya95wXx1ThAddurAvziVBZ8Ekde7sNCA==')})
  }
//]]>
